### Post by ajgreeny on 2015-11-05
You do not have Ubuntu installed, I'm afraid, even though grub is installed in the MBR of sda, your hard disk.

How did you try to install Ubuntu in the first place?

### Post by Arun_Mishra on 2015-11-05
Thanks for replying so fast.

I have Ubuntu installed in /dev/sda3 18.9 GB partition, as you can see in the screen shot below. 

I did a fresh install of Ubuntu 15.10 a couple of days back in /dev/sda3 and was using it today. All of a sudden the system froze and did not respond for half an hour.
So I used the power button to shut down my system and restart it. But after retarting, I am not able to use two partitions sda2 (176 GB) and sda3 (18.9 GB). Both these partitions where open when my system had frozen. So, I guess, it must have to do something with the time my system froze. It might have done some short of damage to my partitions. I have valuable data in both the partitions, especially the 176 GB partition.

### Post by ajgreeny on 2015-11-06
No screenshot shown so I can not go any further, but sda3 is an extended partition containing sda5, which is swap, and sda6, see below, which is unknown and will be your now corrupt Ubuntu partition.
```
sda6: __________________________________________________________________________

    File system:       
    Boot sector type:  Unknown
    Boot sector info: 
    Mounting failed:   mount: unknown filesystem type ''
mount: unknown filesystem type ''
```
Boot to a live ubuntu DVD or USB and open a terminal in that.
Run command ```
sudo e2fsck /dev/sda6
``` and see if any errors appear in the output of that.  That may be all that is required to repair your filesystem.

---

### Post by Arun_Mishra on 2015-11-06
I ran the command on terminal and get the following result

ubuntu@ubuntu:~$ sudo e2fsck /dev/sda6
e2fsck 1.42.12 (29-Aug-2014)
e2fsck: Attempt to read block from filesystem resulted in short read while trying to open /dev/sda6
Could this be a zero-length partition?

I suspect a hardware issue here. Is there any chance to fix such an error. Or should I just try to recover my data somehow and go go for formatting the drive? In the latter case, what is the best way to recover my data?

---

### Post by oldfred on 2015-11-06
In disks is Smart Tools, icon in upper right. That should tell you if drive is good or not.
It can run lots of tests but all I know is that if drive is bad, best to get a new drive.

You can try recovering from another superblock.
       [http://linuxexpresso.wordpress.com/2010/03/31/repair-a-broken-ext4-superblock-in-ubuntu/](http://linuxexpresso.wordpress.com/2010/03/31/repair-a-broken-ext4-superblock-in-ubuntu/)
Remove first inode to use alternative superblock:
[http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1682038](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1682038)
Using alternative superblock to check ext3
[http://planet.admon.org/using-alternative-superblock-to-check-ext3/](http://planet.admon.org/using-alternative-superblock-to-check-ext3/)
List backup superblocks:
sudo dumpe2fs /dev/sda5 | grep -i backup
then use backup superblock, 32768 just an example, try several
sudo fsck -b 32768 /dev/sda6

---

### Post by Arun_Mishra on 2015-11-06
Thanks a lot for your help. I was able to solve the problem with the help of the following link. Although I am not able to boot into the Ubuntu installation anymore, I was able to recover my files through a live CD. And once I fixed the Ubuntu drive, my main 176 GB drive started working without any problems. So, I will go ahead and format the Ubuntu drive.

[https://linuxexpresso.wordpress.com/2010/03/31/repair-a-broken-ext4-superblock-in-ubuntu/](https://linuxexpresso.wordpress.com/2010/03/31/repair-a-broken-ext4-superblock-in-ubuntu/)
